Whitney anukramaс╣З─л

[Brahman.тАФdv─Бviс╣Е┼Ыakam. v─Бm─лyam ─Бdityadevatyam adhy─Бtmakaram. tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham: 12, 14, 16, 18. jagat─л.]

Whitney

Comment

This hymn and the following (except a few verses of the latter) are one Rig-Veda hymn, namely, i. 164, and but a small part of them occur in any other Vedic text. Both are found in P─Бipp. xvi., in somewhat changed verse-order, as will be noted under the different verses below. V─Бit. takes no notice of this hymn; in K─Бu┼Ы. it (vs. 1) is quoted in 18. 25, with various others, in a ceremony for prosperity; and the gaс╣Зam─Бl─Б (see note to K─Бu┼Ы. 18. 25) reckons it as belonging to the salila gaс╣Зa.

Translations

II., Heft 3, f├╝r 1875, M├╝nchen, 1876 (the essay, says Whitney, “casts extremely little light upon its labored obscurities”); further, with an elaborate comment touching the significance of its philosophic content, by Deussen, Geschichte, i. 1. 105-119; parts also by Muir, v. (see Index, p. 484), and Hillebrandt, Ved. Mythol., i. (see Index, p. 542); and under the title, Zwei Spr├╝che ├╝ber Leib und Seele, ZDMG. xlvi. 759 f., Roth explains two verses answering to our ix. 10. 8 and 16. Under the title. Das R├дthsel vom Jahre, ZDMG. xlviii. 353, E. Windisch discusses the RV. verse answering to our vs. 12.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Of this pleasant (v─Бm├б) hoary invokerтАФof him the brother is the
    midmost stone (? ├б┼Ыna); his third brother [is] ghee-backed; there I
    saw the lord of the people who hath seven sons.
Notes

The three brothers are explained as the three forms of Agni, in heaven,
in the atmosphere (lightning), and on earth (sacrificial fire): the
‘seven sons’ are most probably his many flames. тМКThe collocation of
madhyam├│ with bhr─Б╠Бt─Б would seem more natural, considering the phrase
tс╣Ыt─л╠Бyo bhr─Б╠Бt─Б.

Griffith

The second brother of this lovely Hotar, hoary with eld, is the voracious Lightning. The third is he whose back is balmed with butter. Here have I seen the King with seven male children.

рдореВрд▓рдореН (VS)

рд╕реТрдкреНрдд рдпреБреСрдЮреНрдЬрдиреНрддрд┐реТ рд░рдереТрдореЗрдХреСрдЪрдХреНрд░реТрдореЗрдХреЛреТ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реЛреС рд╡рд╣рддрд┐ рд╕реТрдкреНрддрдирд╛реСрдорд╛ред
рддреНрд░рд┐реТрдирд╛рднрд┐реС рдЪреТрдХреНрд░рдореТрдЬрд░реСрдордиреТрд░реНрд╡рдВ рдпрддреНрд░реЗреТрдорд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛реТ рднреБрд╡реТрдирд╛рдзрд┐реС рддреТрд╕реНрдереБрдГ рее

режреи рд╕рдкреНрдд рдпреБрдЮреНрдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Seven harness (yuj) a one-wheeled chariot; one horse, having seven
    names, draws (vah) [it]; of three naves [is] the wheel, unwasting,
    unassailed, whereon stand all these existences.
Notes

Doubtless the sun. The verse is repeated as xiii. 3. 18. It occurs also
in TA. iii. 11. 8, with anarv─Бс╣Б yene тАЩm─Б v. bhuvan─Бni t. in c, d
(the accent of the verse is too corrupt to heed).

Griffith

The seven make the one-wheeled chariot ready: bearing seven names the single Courser draws it. The wheel, three-naved, is sound and undecaying: thereon these worlds of life are all dependent.

рд╕реТрдкреНрддред рдпреБреТрдЮреНрдЬреТрдиреНрддрд┐реТред рд░рдереСрдореНред рдПрдХреСрд╜рдЪрдХреНрд░рдореНред рдПрдХрдГреСред рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдГреСред рд╡реТрд╣реТрддрд┐реТред рд╕реТрдкреНрддрд╜рдирд╛реСрдорд╛ред рддреНрд░рд┐реТрд╜рдирд╛рднрд┐реСред рдЪреТрдХреНрд░рдореНред рдЕреТрдЬрд░реСрдореНред рдЕреТрдиреТрд░реНрд╡рдореНред рдпрддреНрд░реСред рдЗреТрдорд╛ред рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛реСред рднреБрд╡реСрдирд╛ред рдЕрдзрд┐реСред рддреТрд╕реНрдереБрдГред резрек.реиред

Whitney
Translation
  1. The seven that stand on this chariotтАФseven horses draw it,
    seven-wheeled; seven sisters shout at [it] together, where are set
    down the seven names of the kine.
Notes

RV. reads navante in c, and n─Б╠Бma in d.

Griffith

The seven who on this seven-wheeled car are mounted have horses, seven in tale, who draw them onward. Seven sisters utter songs of praise together, in whom the Cows’ seven names are held and treasured.

режрек рдХреЛ рджрджрд░реНрд╢ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Who saw it first in process of birth, as the boneless one bears
    (bhс╣Ы) him that has bones? where forsooth the earth’s life (├бsu),
    blood, soul? who shall go to ask that of him who knows?
Notes

‘Bears,’ not in the sense of ‘gives birth to,’ but of ‘carries’ or
‘supports’ or the like.

Griffith

Who hath beheld at birth the Primal Being, when She who hath no bone supports the bony? Where is the blood of earth, the life, the spirit? Who may ap- proach the man who knows, to ask it?

Whitney
Translation
  1. Simple, not discerning (vi-j├▒─Б) with the mind, I ask about the thus
    set-down tracks of the gods; over the yearling (? baс╣гk├бya) calf have
    the poets stretched out seven lines (t├бntu) for weaving.
Notes
Griffith

Unripe in mind, in spirit undiscerning, I ask of these the Gods’ established places. High up above the yearling Calf the sages, to form a web, their own seven threads have woven.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I, not understanding (cit), ask here the understanding poets, I
    unknowing (vid), them that know; he who propped asunder these six
    spaces (r├бjas), in the form of the goat (? aj├б)тАФwas that also alone?
Notes

The sense of the last p─Бda is utterly obscure, and the version given
only tentative; aj├б is perhaps here really the ‘unborn one,’ as the
translators render it. RV. reads in a ├бcikitv─Б├▒ cik-, and, in
b, vidm├бne, for which our vidv├бnas is apparently a mere
corruption.

Griffith

Here, ignorant, I ask the wise who know it, as one who knows not, for the sake of knowledge, What is That One, who in the Unborn’s image hath stablished and fixed firm this world’s six regions.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The mother portioned the father in righteousness, for with meditation
    (dh─лt├н), with mind, came together in the beginning she, repugnant,
    womb-sapped, pierced; paying homage, verily, they went unto
    encouragement.
Notes

The version is in part only mechanical. Ppp. combines с╣Ыt─Б тАЭbabh- in
a, and reads jaj├▒e at end of b.

Griffith

The Mother gave the Sire his share of Order. With thought at first she wedded him in spirit. She, coyly loth, was filled with dew prolific. With adoration men approached to praise her.

Griffith

Yoked was the Mother to the boon Cow’s car-pole; in humid folds of cloud the infant rested. Then the Calf lowed and looked upon the Mother, the Cow who wears all shapes in three directions.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The one, bearing three mothers [and] three fathers, stood
    upright; verily they do not exhaust him; on the back of yon sky the
    all-knowing ones talk a speech not found by all.
Notes

RV. reads gl─Бpayanti at end of b тМКand the translation follows that
readingтМЛ, and, for d, vi┼Ыvav├нdaс╣Б v─Б╠Бcam ├бvi┼Ыvaminv─Бm. The
pada-text reads glapayanta; Pr─Бt. iv. 93 notes the case. Ppp. agrees
with RV. in gl─Бpayanti and vi┼Ыvavidam.

Griffith

Bearing three mothers and three fathers, single he stood erect: they never made him weary. On yonder heaven’s high ridge they speak together in speech not known to all, themselves all-knowing.

резрез рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд░реЗ рдЪрдХреНрд░реЗ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. On the five-spoked circumvolving wheel on which stood all
    existencesтАФits axle, much-burdened, is not heated; even from of old it
    is not severed with the nave.
Notes

RV. and Ppp. count this verse as 13, our version inverting the order of
11-13. In b, RV. reads t├бsminn ─Б╠Б tasthur bh. v., and Ppp.
sam─Бrohanti bh. v.; and RV. has ┼Ы─лryate for chidyate in d.

Griffith

Upon the five-spoked wheel revolving ever, whereon all crea- tures rest and are dependent, The axle, heavy-laden, is not heated: the nave from ancient time remains unheated.

рдкрдЮреНрдЪреСрд╜рдЕрд░реЗред рдЪреТрдХреНрд░реЗред рдкреТрд░рд┐реТрд╜рд╡рд░реНрддреСрдорд╛рдиреЗред рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐реСрдиреНред рдЖреТрд╜рддреТрд╕реНрдереБрдГред рднреБрд╡реСрдирд╛рдирд┐ред рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛реСред рддрд╕реНрдпреСред рдиред рдЕрдХреНрд╖рдГреСред рддреТрдкреНрдпреТрддреЗреТред рднреВрд░рд┐реСрд╜рднрд╛рд░рдГред рд╕реТрдирд╛рддреНред рдПреТрд╡ред рдиред рдЫрд┐реТрджреНрдпреТрддреЗреТред рд╕рд╜рдирд╛реСрднрд┐рдГред резрек.резрезред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд░реЗ) [рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдЖрджрд┐ рдкрд╛рдБрдЪ рддрддреНрддреНрд╡ рд░реВрдк] рдкрд╛рдБрдЪ рдЕрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рдкрд░рд┐рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗ) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рдШреВрдорддреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) рдЬрд┐рд╕ (рдЪрдХреНрд░реЗ) рдкрд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рдкрд░ [рдкрд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рдЬрдЧрддреН рдореЗрдВ] (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛) рднреБрд╡рдирд╛рдирд┐) рд╕рдм рд▓реЛрдХ (рдЖрддрд╕реНрдереБрдГ) рдард╣рд░реЗ рд╣реБрдП рд╣реИрдВред (рддрд╕реНрдп) рдЙрд╕ [рдЪрдХреНрд░рд░реВрдк рдЬрдЧрддреН] рдХрд╛ (рднреВрд░рд┐рднрд╛рд░рдГ) рдмрдбрд╝реЗ рдмреЛрдЭрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рд╕рдирд╛рднрд┐рдГ) рдирд╛рднрд┐ рдореЗрдВ рд▓рдЧрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ (рдЕрдХреНрд╖рдГ) рдзреБрд░рд╛ [рдзреБрд░рд╛ рд░реВрдк рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░] (рд╕рдирд╛рддреН рдПрд╡) рд╕рджрд╛ рд╕реЗ рд╣реА (рди рддрдкреНрдпрддреЗ) рди рддреЛ рддрдкрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рдФрд░ (рди рдЫрд┐рджреНрдпрддреЗ) рди рдЯреВрдЯрддрд╛ рд╣реИ реерезрезрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА, рдЬрд▓, рддреЗрдЬ, рд╡рд╛рдпреБ рдФрд░ рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢ рдкрд╛рдБрдЪ рднреВрддреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд┐рдд рдЬрдЧрддреН рдореЗрдВ рд╕рдм рд▓реЛрдХ рд╕реНрдерд┐рдд рд╣реИрдВ, рдЙрд╕ рдЬрдЧрддреН рдХрд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА рдЕрдЬрд░-рдЕрдорд░ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рд╣реИред рдФрд░ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд░рде рдореЗрдВ рдЕрдзрд┐рдХ рдмреЛрдЭ рд▓рд╛рджрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдзреБрд░рд╛ рддрдкрдХрд░ рдЯреВрдЯ рдЬрд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдХрд╛ рдЗрддрдирд╛ рдмреЛрдЭ рдЕрдирд╛рджрд┐ рдХрд╛рд▓ рд╕реЗ рдЙрдард╛рдиреЗ рдкрд░ рднреА рдХреНрд▓реЗрд╢ рдирд╣реАрдВ рдкрд╛рддрд╛ реерезрезрее (рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН, рдЫрд┐рджреНрдпрддреЗ) рдХреЗ рд╕реНрдерд╛рди рдкрд░ [рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН, рд╢реАрд░реНрдпрддреЗ] рд╣реИрдВтИТрдЛреж резредрезремрекредрезрей рее

Whitney
Translation
  1. The five-footed father, of twelve shapes (-─Б╠Бkс╣Ыti), they call rich
    in ground (pur─лс╣г├нn) in the far (p├бra) half of the sky; then these
    others call [him] set (├бrpita) in the lower outlook that is
    seven-wheeled, six-spoked.
Notes

RV. and Ppp. have the easier and better reading vicakс╣гaс╣З├бm in c,
and Ppp. reads before it upari. тМКThe Kaс╣нha reading also is ├║pari,
WZKM. xii. 282.тМЛ Read in b p├бre (an accent sign slipped out of
place). тМКSee Roth, KZ. xxvi. 66, and Windisch as cited in the
introduction; cf. also IFA. vi. 181, as noted above.тМЛ

Griffith

They call him in the farther half of heaven the Sire five-footed, of twelve forms, wealthy in watery store. These others, later still, say that he takes his stand upon a seven- wheeled car, six-spoked, whose sight is clear.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The twelve-spoked wheelтАФfor that is not to be worn outтАФrevolves
    greatly about the sky of righteousness; there, O Agni, stood the sons,
    paired, seven hundred and twenty.
Notes

Here the ’twelve’ and the ‘seven hundred and twenty’ are plainly the
months, and the days and nights, of the year of 360 days. The verse, as
noted above, is vs. 11 in RV. and Ppp. The more proper reading in b
would be v├бrvartti.

Griffith

Formed with twelve spokes, too strong for age to weaken, this wheel of during Order rolls round heaven. Herein established, joined in pairs together, seven hundred sons and twenty stand, O Agni.

резрек рд╕рдиреЗрдорд┐ рдЪрдХреНрд░рдордЬрд░рдореН ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. The unwasting wheel, with rim, rolls about; ten harnessed ones draw
    upon the outstretched one (fem.); the sun’s eye goes surrounded with the
    welkin (r├бjas), in which stood all existences.
Notes

Ppp. has vrajanti for vahanti in b, and, for d yasminn
─Бrpit─Б bhuvan─Бny ─Бrpit─Б; RV. has t├бsminn ─Б╠Бrpit─Б for our y├бsminn
─Бtasth├║с╕е. The Anukr. calls the verse simply a jagat─л, though only two
of its p─Бdas have 12 syllables.

Griffith

The wheel revolves, unwasting, with its felly: ten draw it, yoked to the far-stretching car-pole. Girt by the region moves the eye of Surya, on whom dependent rest all living creatures.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Them, being women, they declared (ah) to me to be men; he who hath
    eyes may see, [but] the blind will not distinguish (vi-cit); the son
    that is a poet, he verily understood (─Б-cit); whoever knows those
    things apart, he shall be [his] father’s father.
Notes

RV. and Ppp. put this verse after our vs. 16. It is found also in TA. i.
11. 4, with t─Б╠Б u in a, im─Б╠Бs in c for ─лm ─Б╠Б, and savit├║с╕е
p- in d. Some of our mss. (P.s.m.O.K.T.) reads pit├║с╕е p- in d;
we had the phrase once before, at ii. 1. 2, and the combination falls
under Pr─Бt. ii. 73. We might expect, in d, t─Б╠Бс╕е, referring to
str├нyaс╕е, but the pada-texts have t─Б╠Б, as neuter pl.

Griffith

They told me these were males, though truly females. He who hath eyes sees this, the blind discerns not. The son who is a sage hath comprehended: who knows this rightly is his father’s father.

Translation
  1. Of those born together the seventh they call sole-born; six, they
    say, are twins, god-born seers; the sacrifices (? iс╣гс╣н├б) of them,
    distributed according to their abodes, quake in their station, being
    altered (vi-kс╣Ы) in respect to form.

should expect instead the ablative. тМКThe vs. recurs at TA. i. 3. 1 with

Griffith

Of the co-born they call the seventh single-born: the six twin, pairs are called the Rishis, sons of Gods. Their good gifts sought of men are ranged in order due, and, various, form by form, move for their guiding Lord.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Below the distant (p├бra), thus beyond the lower, bearing (bhс╣Ы)
    her calf with her foot, the cow hath stood up; whitherwards, to what
    quarter (├бrdha) hath she forsooth gone away? where giveth she birth?
    for [it is] not in this herd.
Notes

The Anukr. takes no notice of the redundant syllable in a; we may
suppose par├б en─Б╠Б- to be combined to par─Б├н тАЩn─Б╠Б-. тМКThe verse is
repeated below as xiii. 1. 41. RV. ends with ant├бс╕е for asm├нn. The
Kaс╣нha variant p├бr─Бk─Бt for p├бr─Бg─Бt (WZKM. xii. 282) shows an exchange
of surd and sonant, the reverse of that noted at ii. 13. 3.тМЛ

Griffith

Beneath the upper realm, above this lower, bearing her Calf at foot, the Cow hath risen. Whitherward, to what place hath she departed? Where doth she calve? Not in this herd of cattle.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╡рддреНрд╕рдореН) [рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕рд╕реНрдерд╛рди] рджреЗрд╣ рдХреЛ (рдмрд┐рднреНрд░рддреА) рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддреА рд╣реБрдИ (рдЧреМрдГ) рдЧреМ [рдЧрддрд┐рд╢реАрд▓ рдЬреАрд╡рд░реВрдк рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐] (рдкрд░реЗрдг) рдКрдБрдЪреЗ (рдкрджрд╛) рдкрдж [рдЕрдзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░ рд╡рд╛ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ] рд╕реЗ (рдЕрд╡рдГ) рдиреАрдЪреЗ рдХреЛ, рдФрд░ (рдПрдирд╛) рдЗрд╕ (рдЕрд╡рд░реЗрдг) рдиреАрдЪреЗ [рдкрдж] рд╕реЗ (рдкрд░рдГ) рдКрдкрд░ рдХреЛ (рдЙрддреН рдЕрд╕реНрдерд╛рддреН) рдЙрдареА рд╣реИред (рд╕рд╛) рд╡рд╣ [рдЬреАрд╡рд░реВрдк рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐] (рдХрджреНрд░реАрдЪреА) рдХрд┐рд╕ рдУрд░ рдЪрд▓рддреА рд╣реБрдИ, (рдХрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд┐рддреН) рдХреМрди рд╕реЗ (рдЕрд░реНрдзрдореН) рдЛрджреНрдзрд┐рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ [рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░] рдХреЛ (рдкрд░рд╛) рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдо рд╕реЗ (рдЕрдЧрд╛рддреН) рдкрд╣реБрдБрдЪреА рд╣реИ, (рдХреНрд╡ рд╕реНрд╡рд┐рддреН) рдХрд╣рд╛рдБ рдкрд░ (рд╕реВрддреЗ) рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рд╣реЛрддреА рд╣реИ, (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) рдЗрд╕ [рджреЗрд╣рдзрд╛рд░реА] (рдпреВрдереЗ) рд╕рдореВрд╣ рдореЗрдВ рддреЛ (рдирд╣рд┐) рдирд╣реАрдВ [рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рд╣реЛрддреА] реерезренрее

Whitney
Translation
  1. Below the distant whoever knows his father, below the distant, thus
    beyond the lowerтАФwho, playing the poet, shall proclaim [him] here?
    from whence [is] heavenly mind produced?
Notes

RV. and Ppp. read, in a, b, y├│ asy─Б тАЩnuv├йda par├б en─Б╠Б-, rectifying
the meter and lightening the construction. Only the first two p─Бdas have
any “jagat─л” character, and they are very irregular. But by giving
this name the Anukr. shows that it reads our version; in RV. and Ppp.
the verse is a pure triс╣гс╣нubh. Read in d k├║to (for kс╣Ы╠Бto).

Griffith

Who, that the father of this Calf discerneth beneath the upper realm, above the lower, Showing himself a sage, may here declare him? Whence hath the godlike spirit had its rising?

рдЕреТрд╡рдГред рдкрд░реЗреСрдгред рдкрд┐реТрддрд░реСрдореНред рдпрдГред рдЕреТрд╕реНрдпреТред рд╡реЗрджреСред рдЕреТрд╡рдГред рдкрд░реЗреСрдгред рдкреТрд░рдГред рдПреТрдирд╛ред рдЕрд╡реСрд░реЗрдгред рдХреТрд╡рд┐реТрд╜рдпрдорд╛реСрдирдГред рдХрдГред рдЗреТрд╣ред рдкреНрд░ред рд╡реЛреТрдЪреТрддреНред рджреЗреТрд╡рдореНред рдордирдГреСред рдХреБрддрдГреСред рдЕрдзрд┐реСред рдкреНрд░рд╜рдЬрд╛реСрддрдореНред резрек.резреоред

рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдФрд░ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЗ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХрд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрдГ) рдЬреЛ [рдкреБрд░реБрд╖] (рдПрдирд╛) рдЗрд╕ (рдЕрд╡рд░реЗрдг) рдиреАрдЪреЗ [рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ] рд╕реЗ (рдкрд░рдГ) рдКрдкрд░ [рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рди], (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) рдЗрд╕ [рджреЗрд╣] рдХреЗ (рдкрд┐рддрд░рдореН) рдкрд╛рд▓рдХ [рдЖрддреНрдорд╛] рдХреЛ (рдкрд░реЗрдг) рдКрдБрдЪреЗ [рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ] рд╕реЗ (рдЕрд╡рдГ) рдиреАрдЪреЗ, (рдкрд░реЗрдг) рдКрдБрдЪреЗ [рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ] рд╕реЗ (рдЕрдЪрдГ) рдиреАрдЪреЗ (рд╡реЗрдж) рдЬрд╛рдирддрд╛ рд╣реИред (рдХрд╡реАрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ) рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдорд╛рдиреН рдХрд╛ рд╕рд╛ рдЖрдЪрд░рдг рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рдХрдГ) рдХреМрди [рдкреБрд░реБрд╖] (рдЗрд╣) рдЗрд╕ [рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп] рдореЗрдВ (рдкреНрд░ рд╡реЛрдЪрддреН) рдмреЛрд▓реЗ? рдФрд░ (рдХреБрддрдГ) рдХрд╣рд╛рдБ рд╕реЗ [рдЙрд╕рдХрд╛] (рджреЗрд╡рдореН) рджрд┐рд╡реНрдп рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рдордирдГ) рдорди [рдордирди рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдп] (рдЕрдзрд┐) рдЕрдзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХ (рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рддрдореН) рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди [рд╣реЛрд╡реЗ ?] реерезреорее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

резреп рдпреЗ рдЕрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдЮреНрдЪрд╕реНрддрд╛рдБ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Them that are hitherward they call off-ward; them, again, that are
    off-ward they call hitherward; what things, O Soma, thou and Indra have
    done, those they draw, harnessed as it were with the pole of the welkin.
Notes

The verse is found also in JB. i. 279, with no various readings that are
not evident corruptions. The ’them’ of a, b is masc., probably the
same with the ’they’ of d (yukt─Б╠Бс╕е, p.). Ppp. reads niyukt─Б
instead of na yukt─Б.

Griffith

Those that come hitherward they call departing, those that depart they call directed hither. Whatever ye have made, Indra and Soma! steeds draw, as’ twere, yoked to the region’s car-pole.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Two eagles (suparс╣З├б), joint companions, embrace the same tree; of
    them the one eats the sweet berry; the other looks on all the time, not
    partaking.
Notes

Ppp. reads in a suyuj─Б. Here and in the next verse, as everywhere
else, some of our mss. read p├нс╣гpalam. тМКThe vs. plays a r├┤le in the
Upanishads: cf. ┼Ыvet. iv. 6; Muс╣Зс╕Н. iii. 1. 1. Hillebrandt, Ved.
Mythol., i. 466, 399, treats this and the following vss.тМЛ

Griffith

Two Birds with fair wings, knit with bonds of friendship, in the same sheltering tree have found a refuge, One of the twain eats the sweet Fig-tree’s berry: the other, eat- ing not, regardeth only.

Translation
  1. On what tree the honey-eating eagles all settle and give birthтАФwhat
    they call the sweet berry in the top of it, that cannot he attain who
    knoweth not [his] father.
Notes

RV. has ├нd ─Бhuс╕е instead of y├бd ─Бh├║с╕е in c, and so also Ppp. (but
─Бhuс╣г). In RV. this verse follows after our vs. 22. There is a
redundant syllable in c of which the Anukr. takes no notice (and the
p─Бda is also capable of being crowded together into eleven syllables).

Griffith

The tree whereon the fine Birds eat the sweetness, where they all rest and procreate their offspring Upon the top, they say the fruit is luscious: none gaineth it who knoweth not the Father.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрддреНрд░) рдЬрд┐рд╕ (рд╡рд┐рджрдерд╛) рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХреЗ рднреАрддрд░ (рд╕реБрдкрд░реНрдгрд╛рдГ) рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ [рд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рдЧрддрд┐рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ, рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреА] (рдЕрдореГрддрд╕реНрдп) рдЕрдореГрддрдкрди [рдореЛрдХреНрд╖рд╕реБрдЦ] рдХреЗ (рднрдХреНрд╖рдореН) рднреЛрдЧ рдХреЛ (рдЕрдирд┐рдореЗрд╖рдореН) рд▓рдЧрд╛рддрд╛рд░ (рдЕрднрд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдиреНрддрд┐) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ рдкрд╛рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВред (рдПрдирд╛) рдЗрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп) рд╕рдм (рднреБрд╡рдирд╕реНрдп) рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░ рдХрд╛ (рдЧреЛрдкрд╛рдГ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХ (рд╕рдГ) рд╡рд╣ (рдзреАрд░рдГ) рдзреАрд░ [рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдорд╛рдиреН рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░] (рдкрд╛рдХрдореН) рдкрдХреНрдХреЗ рдордирд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рдорд╛) рдореБрдЭ рдореЗрдВ (рдЕрддреНрд░) рдЗрд╕ [рджреЗрд╣] рдХреЗ рднреАрддрд░ (рдЖ) рдпрдерд╛рд╡рддреН (рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрд╢) рдкреИрдард╛ рд╣реИ реереиреирее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬрд┐рд╕ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдпреЛрдЧреА рдЬрди рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рд╕реЗ рдореЛрдХреНрд╖ рд╕реБрдЦ рднреЛрдЧрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпреЗрдХ рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рдХ рджреГрдврдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рд╣реЛ рдореЛрдХреНрд╖ рд╕реБрдЦ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░реЗ реереиреирее рдпрд╣ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдирд┐рд░реБрдХреНрдд рейредрезреиред рдореЗрдВ рднреА рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдд рд╣реИ рее (рднрдХреНрд╖рдореН, рдПрдирд╛) рдХреЗ рд╕реНрдерд╛рди рдкрд░ [рднрд╛рдЧрдореН, рдЗрдирдГ] рдкрдж рд╣реИрдВ, рдЛрдЧреНрд╡реЗрдж рдордиреНрддреНрд░ реирез рее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рдкрд╛рджрдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: реиреитИТ(рдпрддреНрд░) рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреЗ (рд╕реБрдкрд░реНрдгрд╛рдГ) рдореж реирезред рд╕реБрдкрд╛рд▓рдХрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдирдГред рд╢реЛрднрдирдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгреЛ рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рдГ-рджреж (рдЕрдореГрддрд╕реНрдп) рдореЛрдХреНрд╖рд╕реНрдп-рджреж (рднрдХреНрд╖рдореН) рднреЛрдЧрдореН (рдЕрдирд┐рдореЗрд╖рдореН) рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░рдореН (рд╡рд┐рджрдерд╛) рд░реБрд╡рд┐рджрд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдЩрд┐рддреНред рдЙреж рейредрезрезрелред рд╡рд┐рдж рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреЗ-рдЕрдеред рд╡реЗрджреЗрди рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреЗрди (рдЕрднрд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдиреНрддрд┐) рд╕реНрд╡рд░рддрд┐рд░реНрдЧрддрд┐рдХрд░реНрдорд╛-рдирд┐рдШреж реиредрезрекред рдЕрднрд┐рдкреНрд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐-рдирд┐рд░реБреж рейредрезреиред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ (рдПрдирд╛) рдПрдиреЗрди рд╡рд┐рджрдереЗрди (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп) рд╕рдордЧреНрд░рд╕реНрдп (рднреБрд╡рдирд╕реНрдп) рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░рд╕реНрдп (рдЧреЛрдкрд╛рдГ) рдЧреЛрдкрд╛рдпрд┐рддрд╛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛ (рд╕рдГ) (рдорд╛) рдорд╛рдореН (рдзреАрд░рдГ) рдзреАрдорд╛рдиреН-рдирд┐рд░реБреж рейредрез┬Шреиред рдзреНрдпрд╛рдирд╡рд╛рдиреН-рджреж (рдкрд╛рдХрдореН) рдкрд╛рдХрдГ рдкрдХреНрддрд╡реНрдпреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдкрдХреНрд╡рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮ рдЖрддреНрдорд╛-рдирд┐рд░реБреж рейредрезреиред рдкрд░рд┐рдкрдХреНрд╡рдордирд╕реНрдХрдореН (рдЕрддреНрд░) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рджреЗрд╣реЗ (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрд╢) рдкреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╢рддрд┐ рее
